City Chamber of Commerce Petitions Government to Improve the Method of Returning Factories: Losses Borne by the People, Benefits Fully Enjoyed by the Nation 96

[This Newspaper Report] The City Chamber of Commerce, based on a proposal from the Shanghai Paper Industry Association, intends to request the government to change the principles for taking over enemy and puppet assets. It sent a telegram to the Executive Yuan a few days ago. The full text is as follows: To the esteemed Executive Yuan of Nanjing, the Chamber of Commerce convened the ninth members' meeting on June 23. According to the proposal of the Shanghai Paper Industry Association, it is intended to request the government to change the principles for taking over enemy and puppet industries. The reasons stated within are: upon investigation, each factory in the recovered areas was forcibly seized by the enemy and puppet regimes, occupied for eight years. The factory buildings and machinery were occupied, and the raw materials and finished products were plundered. (Omission)

Heavy Losses Make Production Impossible

After the factories are taken over, resuming production requires painstaking management. Given the post-disaster situation, with a hundred holes and thousands of wounds, for the sake of economic recovery and promoting production, the government should provide assistance and encouragement to achieve the goal of national construction. However, it is heard that the Ministry of Economic Affairs and the Enemy and Puppet Property Administration Bureau are handling the return of private factories based on the condition that only the undamaged machinery and equipment are returned. The raw materials, finished products, and materials stored in the factory when it was taken over must be nationalized. Even the factory buildings and equipment that were dismantled and transformed by the enemy must be considered as newly added or installed by the enemy, and the original owners must be charged for them.

Nominal Return, Only the Shell Remains

Under this situation, the nominal return of private factories only leaves the shell. Without newly adding raw materials and materials, it is impossible to start work and maintain production. (Omission) Logically speaking, the factory land and machinery and equipment are the mother of production. Because the enemy occupied private factories, the added raw materials, manufactured goods, and transformed equipment are all interdependent, like mother and child, and cannot be separated. In other words, the occupation of private factories is the cause, and the aforementioned products are the result. They should naturally be enjoyed by the original factory owners who were occupied, and should not be regarded as war trophies of the state. Among them, there are factories whose raw materials and finished products stored in the factory when they were occupied were also plundered by the enemy. If the current proposed method is followed, the losses will be borne by the people, and while it is nominally possible to claim compensation from Japan in the future, it is actually far off and amounts to quenching thirst with plums. The benefits will be enjoyed by the state, and a part of the people's losses will be divided as the state's exclusive benefit. Considering that the state and the people originally belong to one body, sharing weal and woe, this is completely contrary. It is proposed that the general assembly suggest that the government change the principles for handling the takeover of enemy and puppet properties.

Proper Method, Recommended for Implementation

All raw materials, materials, finished products, and newly added or transformed equipment taken over from occupied private factories should be handed over to the original factory for valuation and used to offset the losses caused by the enemy's occupation, seizure, and destruction. If there is any surplus, it can be nationalized and deposited in the treasury, but a reasonable deadline should be given for phased repayment to benefit recovery and production. (Omission) It is found that this case was previously forwarded to the National Political Council for a proposal. The Executive Yuan replied to the Secretariat of the National Political Council, stating that the Nationwide Enterprise Takeover Committee in the recovered areas had reviewed and decided that if the original telegram from the City Chamber of Commerce was followed, not only would the occupied factories that had already been processed by various administrations have to be re-liquidated, but the future work of clearing and claiming compensation from Japan would also be fragmented. It requested instructions on whether to approve the request, or to give each occupied factory the right to prioritize claims and compensation when handling compensation from Japan. The Executive Yuan rejected the matter based on the council's decision, and the Secretariat of the National Political Council forwarded the reply to the City Chamber of Commerce. The council's reply only focused on the difficulties in official procedures, and did not consider the points in the original telegram that "the occupation of private factories is the cause, and the aforementioned products are the result, they should naturally be enjoyed by the original factory owners who were occupied, and should not be regarded as war trophies of the state," and "the nominal return of private factories only leaves the shell," and "if the current proposed method is followed, the losses will be borne by the people."

Claims from Japan are Distant and Uncertain

"While it is nominally possible to claim compensation from Japan in the future, it is actually far off." In the council's reply, Item 445, these were not taken into account at all. It only knows how to plan from the perspective of public interest, which is not the position that a country should have, with the people as the basis. In accordance with the public opinion of the industry, a renewed request is made, hoping that the esteemed Executive Yuan will review, approve, and implement it. (Omission)

Report from Zhejiang Administrative Conference - Our Newspaper's Hangzhou Dispatch, 12th Day - Special Correspondent Chu Yusheng 104

Unfolding China's landmass, on the southeastern edge lies a peach-shaped area, smaller in area than any other piece of land; this is Zhejiang Province. The total area of Zhejiang Province is 153,968,424 *shi mu*. Although the area isn't large, it has 21,762,248 people. On average, each person has 7.7 *shi mu* of land. As Shen Honglie said, "Zhejiang is a healthy person. The people have a relatively high level of knowledge, and their lives are quite good." Indeed, Zhejiang's land is fertile, its agricultural products are abundant, and coupled with its geographical proximity to the sea, it produces many outstanding talents.

Warm Hometown: Zhejiang

In a healthy province, the male and female population statistics should not differ greatly. Zhejiang has 11,758,194 men and 10,004,054 women, a difference of just over a million. The proportions are not far apart. Due to the relatively similar male and female ratios, a simple and unadorned social custom prevails. There are few frivolous women and few shallow men. Moreover, the entire territory consists of arable land, with 37,790,697 *shi mu* of farmland and 100,912,934 *shi mu* of mountainous land. There are no barren, deforested mountains; instead, there are lush forests, providing resources for production. With just a little effort, one can obtain enough to be fed and clothed. The transportation within the province is also very developed, with 301,791 *shi mu* of roads and 3,578,653 *shi mu* of rivers and lakes. Besides trains and automobiles on land, there are various human-powered vehicles. Besides steamers and motorized boats on waterways, there are various boats of different sizes. Therefore, many people come to Zhejiang from afar, lingering in this warm hometown of abundant food and clothing.

Fallen into an Abyss of Suffering

For the past eight or nine years, the flames of war have spread throughout Zhejiang Province. Thirty counties fell into enemy hands, and nine were recovered. In the thirty-first year, twenty-two counties fell, and fifteen were recovered. In the thirty-second year, thirty-nine counties fell. After bloody struggles, twenty-nine counties were recovered. This repeated falling and recovery brought the entire production to a standstill. People fled their original posts, and coupled with the layers of exploitation by the enemy and puppet regimes, a beautiful Zhejiang was transformed into a tattered ruin riddled with holes. Eagerly awaiting the arrival of victory, the "selfishness" and "negligence" of the officials caused Zhejiang to fall into an abyss of suffering once again. The people of Zhejiang urgently long for good governance by officials more than anything else. Indeed, in the county seats of Zhejiang today, there are many dilapidated walls and ruins. In the countryside, there are many barren fields. The people cannot make a living, and those who resort to desperate measures are everywhere.

A Landmark Important Conference

Chairman Shen Honglie of Zhejiang, upon taking office, inspected the seawalls and urged their urgent repair. Then, he inspected various counties to learn about the people's suffering. Upon returning, he explained the importance of recovery. He revealed that this year's priorities were public security, followed by relief, and then transportation. Next year, he aimed to have each county effectively assume its responsibility for security, and each township to achieve the goal of education. He also broadly promoted water conservancy loans. At the same time, he believed that the current natural disasters were caused by the gradual deforestation, so he planned to focus on agricultural production in the western Zhejiang plains and on afforestation in the eastern Zhejiang mountains, dredging various rivers and streams to prevent a recurrence of future disasters. He also did not advocate empty talk, striving for practicality. This year, he would consolidate the generally good situation and then seek development, rather than focusing on immediate attractive figures and reports, but rather on practical content. Shen Honglie is indeed doing this, and doing it tirelessly. I interviewed the respected and upright Mr. Zhu Xianwen, the Speaker of the Zhejiang Provincial Provisional Assembly, who told me, "Chairman Shen can be considered diligent in his duties and loving to the people." We welcome a good official who is diligent in his duties and loves the people. Conversely, we oppose a "negligent" and "selfish" corrupt official. We want to see Mr. Shen continue to work actively. On the 20th of this month, Mr. Shen will convene a provincial administrative conference in Hangzhou, which can be considered a landmark and important conference in Zhejiang's politics. The past is gone; we wish to encourage those who come after!

Public Security, Officialdom, Relief

According to Chairman Shen's disclosure: Zhejiang Province prioritizes public security this year, because only after the public security problem is resolved can the people truly recover. This is indeed an enlightened view. However, this reporter believes that during the maintenance of public security, it is even more necessary to concurrently address the clarification of officialdom. Because if officialdom is not clarified, then in addition to visible bandits, there will still be invisible bandits. Invisible bandits can lead to visible bandits. Chairman Shen has declared that he will not use personal connections, and up to now, he has indeed not used any personal connections. We believe that Chairman Shen is determined to clarify officialdom. However, the prerequisite for clarifying officialdom is to improve the treatment of public officials. Currently, senior county-level officials receive only 50,000 yuan per month. How can they support a family? Regarding this, we hope that there will be a concrete resolution in this administrative conference.

Chairman Shen also revealed that another important goal this year is relief, such as solving the universal problems of food, clothing, and shelter in thousands of counties. If the problems of food, clothing, and shelter cannot be solved, all public security measures are empty. This is also a crucial plan. However, solving the problems of food, clothing, and shelter is indeed not an easy task. We hope that each district and county will have a concrete plan to submit for everyone to study. We know that this relief plan must first have money. Zhejiang Province is now truly in dire straits, with its finances stretched to the limit. Where will this huge sum of money come from? If each district and county has a meticulous plan, perhaps using work as relief, or intensifying production, there may be a chance of success. Therefore, we are willing to learn of feasible relief plans in this administrative conference.

Sluggish Export Products

This province was originally a society with abundant agricultural products. Geographically speaking, Zhejiang is not suitable for industry but suitable for agriculture. Its agricultural products, in addition to grains, wheat, and beans, also include tung oil and tea leaves, which are all major export products. These many export products are now on the verge of stagnation. How should they be improved? How should production be increased? How can people who produce these many products live and work in peace? This is indeed a very important issue at present. We know that these many products can also be industrialized, that is, the original agricultural products can be processed through industry and then sold abroad. However, these plans require people with great courage and foresight to implement them. We hope that each district and county will study these special products with past export achievements and provide concrete opinions, because the result of these exports is also to increase the wealth of Zhejiang.

The administrative conference will be attended by more than 130 people, including provincial government members, department heads, district commissioners, county magistrates, and section chiefs and above from various departments and bureaus, for ten days. During these ten days, we believe that there will be very good resolutions, especially since Chairman Shen has provided appropriate suggestions in advance. Following these suggestions, there will definitely be good opinions. "Zhejiang is a healthy person," but now it is suffering from a serious typhoid fever. Officials are originally doctors, and the administrative conference is equivalent to a doctors' conference. Let's see what good medicine this doctors' conference will use to treat this seriously ill patient? What good prescription will be implemented to perform the art of resuscitation?

Anti-Treason Work in Hong Kong 105

— Special Correspondent Lin Youlan, Hong Kong Dispatch, 13th Day of This Month

At the beginning of this article, the reporter would like to specifically explain the meaning of "traitor" (奸): Because the connotation of this word "traitor" may be different in Hong Kong and in the mainland. This difference is precisely the point of this article. In Hong Kong, the objects betrayed by a "traitor" are divided into (1) the Allied nations (including China and Britain), (2) Britain, and (3) China. The first type is called a "war criminal," the second is called an "enemy collaborator," and the third is called a "Han traitor" (漢奸) - the Han traitor referred to in our country's regulations for punishing Han traitors refers to this type. This article will also discuss the progress of the anti-traitor campaign in Hong Kong based on this distinction.

War Criminals on Trial

According to an announcement by the British Army Headquarters in Hong Kong, there are currently more than 200 war criminals imprisoned in Chi Ma Wan Prison. How does Hong Kong interpret "war criminal"? According to the chief prosecutor at the public trial of the first batch of war criminals by the Hong Kong Army Military Tribunal, international law stipulates that the most important actions of an occupier should be to respect the lives of the local people, not to disturb their peaceful lives, not to interfere with their religious beliefs, and not to threaten them with illegal or criminal charges. Anyone who fails to comply with these rules is in violation of the law and against the customs of war, and is regarded as the most important major war criminal. All the people belonging to this category are Japanese soldiers.

From the public trial of the first batch of war criminals on March 28 to the present date of the draft, six batches have been tried, totaling 23 war criminals. Five were sentenced to death, and the rest were sentenced to imprisonment, ranging from eight years to as little as two years.

The public trial of war criminals is the same as the public trial of other criminals, allowing civilians to observe. However, war criminals are only tried once by a military tribunal, and a judgment can be made immediately. "Enemy collaborators," however, are tried twice, first by the magistrate's court - called the Summary Court during the military administration - and then by the High Court. Although there are witnesses giving testimony and defense lawyers making arguments, the procedure is relatively fast. From the day of arraignment to the day of judgment, it takes no more than a month, so six batches were tried within 100 days. Although four batches of enemy collaborators have been brought to court, the first batch of six people has not been adjudicated yet, due to individual trials. The public trials of the various batches of war criminals are briefly described below:

(1) The first batch of 15 war criminals was charged with torturing and killing residents of Silvermine Bay, Lantau Island, from August 18 to August 26, 1945. The trial began on March 28 and ended on April 25: Lieutenant Abo Yasuo (commander of the Japanese army squadron stationed there), Lieutenant Matsumoto, and Sergeant Uchida were sentenced to death. Warrant Officer Yanagisawa and Corporal Kamishiro were sentenced to ten years' imprisonment. Sergeant Yoshikawa was sentenced to eight years' imprisonment. Sergeant Kodama was sentenced to five years' imprisonment. Sergeant Sukito, Corporal Jun Take, Corporal Nishizawa, and Corporal Uemura and Corporal Okamoto were sentenced to two years' imprisonment. Warrant Officer Ando, Sergeant Shiromori, and Private First Class Takahashi were acquitted and released.

(2) War criminal Matsuda Kenichi, a sergeant in the Japanese military police, nicknamed "Tiger Boy," was sentenced on May 10 to eight years' imprisonment for torturing a Chinese man, Li Jinman, to death. The verdict was on May 14.

(3) War criminal Inoue Kinio, an interpreter for the Japanese military police, nicknamed "King of Torture," was charged on May 22 with torturing prisoners of war and civilians and sentenced to death on May 27.

(4) Four war criminals, Japanese military police, were charged on May 30 with torturing seven Chinese people. On June 11, the verdicts were: Corporal Sano sentenced to eight years' imprisonment, Warrant Officer Kurosawa sentenced to six years' imprisonment, Sergeant Iida (nicknamed "Watering King of South China") sentenced to three years' imprisonment, and Sergeant Sakamoto acquitted.

(5) War criminal Omura Kiyoshi, a warrant officer in the Japanese military police, was charged on July 2 with torturing six Chinese people and sentenced to seven years' imprisonment on July 4.

(6) War criminal Sergeant Kawamoto of the Japanese military police was charged on July 9 with torturing a British man to death and sentenced to death on July 10.

Nono Kenosuke, the former commander of the Japanese military police in Hong Kong, Major General Okada, who represented the Japanese army in Hong Kong in the surrender, and Lieutenant General Sakai Takashi, who commanded the Japanese army's attack on Hong Kong, have also been listed as war criminals in Hong Kong. The Hong Kong Army Military Tribunal is currently collecting evidence. Except for Sakai Takashi, who is being tried in Nanjing by our country, the other criminals will be brought to trial one after another in the coming days.

Enemy Collaborators

The Hong Kong government formally announced on February 7: All those who "during the Japanese occupation, adhered to or assisted the Japanese; or acted in a way that was detrimental to the war aims of the Allied nations; or who committed offenses against the defense laws of the Hong Kong government; or who committed serious crimes against the criminal laws of Hong Kong" shall all be treated as war criminals (War Criminals). In this way, war criminals are no different from what our country refers to as "Han traitors." When the first enemy collaborator, Huang Zuo, was publicly tried, the chief prosecutor formally defined High Treason for enemy collaborators as "committing treason against the 1351 Treason Act (Edward III, Chapter 2) within the territory of Hong Kong and its dependencies." In other words, those who were disloyal to the British Crown or "who acted as traitors when the British Crown and its subjects were openly at war with the Japanese military and civilians." Therefore, there is a prerequisite for enemy collaborators: he or she must be British, or have British nationality, or at least have sworn allegiance to the British Crown. Because of this key point, Huang Zuo's defense lawyer made a lengthy argument: Huang is Chinese and should not be governed by British law. He also said that Hong Kong was no longer a British territory after its fall, but a Japanese-occupied territory, and its residents were not required to be loyal to the British Crown. Xu Guozhen's defense lawyer, another enemy collaborator, also said: "The defendant is not a British citizen. All Chinese people are free to travel between China and Hong Kong. It can be argued that Chinese people in Hong Kong do not have to be loyal to the British Crown."

On the eve of the war criminals' trial, the authorities specially displayed 168 photographs of war criminals in two batches in central locations in order to collect evidence from the general public. In Chinese and English, it said: "Do you know him?" and "If you have information about any of them committing war crimes, such as brutal acts, torture, etc., please write down the photograph number and come to Room 305, 4th Floor, HSBC Building." However, there was no such procedure for the trial of enemy collaborators. Most of the witnesses who testified in court about the past enemy collaboration activities of the enemy collaborators were British intelligence agents and their families who had been tortured by the enemy collaborators. One of them was even the government prosecutor who is now serving in court. After Li Jie, one of the enemy collaborators, was sentenced to death, he angrily defended himself in court: "I feel extremely unfair about the verdict, because the statements made by the various witnesses contain many errors and are mostly fabricated. Although I am now sentenced to death, I am not afraid of death. However, I am extremely eager to make the whole story of this case public to society, so that people of reason in society can make a fair judgment. What I find even more unfair is that there are many more important traitors in Hong Kong who are still at large, or have been arrested but ultimately released, while insignificant people like me are being severely punished."

Huang Zuo, the first enemy collaborator, was hanged at Stanley Prison on July 10. - He was the second person to be hanged after the British army re-entered Hong Kong. The first was an adopted son who killed his adoptive mother. According to the list of the first batch of enemy collaborators published by the Hong Kong government, there are six in total. In addition to Huang Zuo, there are also Su Liang, Xu Guozhen, Li Jie, Li Caishi (Portuguese), and Jining (Swedish). Since being brought to court on February 19, they have been individually tried in public. Huang was charged with a total of thirty-one counts of crimes. Xu confessed that the former Mayor of Guangzhou, "Chen Ce, was his indirect superior" and was sentenced to death on July 27. Su Liang is still on trial. Li Jie, nicknamed "Number One Secret Agent of Kowloon," "whose brutal behavior was even worse than the enemy's," was sentenced to death on May 30. Li Caishi, who was accused of "colluding with the enemy to bring the Xian ship from Australia to Hong Kong," is still in custody awaiting trial. Jining, who was accused of "directing the enemy artillery in Kowloon to use Hong Kong as a target for shooting," was acquitted at the public trial on April 17 because his defense lawyer argued that "according to the British government's grace measures, those suspected of assisting the enemy, but found to have no brutal behavior, cannot be prosecuted." This grace measure has benefited many other "enemy collaborators" who have not yet been announced! But Jining was ultimately deported from Hong Kong for life by the Hong Kong government.

The second batch of enemy collaborators consists of five Indians and two Chinese. The third batch consists of three Westerners, one Indian, and five Chinese. The fourth batch consists of nine Chinese. All of these have been brought to court one after another. Except for the three Westerners who have been released on bail, none of the other prisoners have been convicted. According to a report on May 4, the authorities were preparing to deport a batch of enemy collaborators, including four Westerners, one Indian, and ten Chinese. Some of those who are being held in prison have already shouted out to request that the judge make a speedy judgment this month.

An Interesting Episode at the British Commonwealth Conference 106

There was an interesting episode at the Commonwealth Conference: When British Prime Minister Attlee announced in the House of Commons that Britain was preparing to completely withdraw its troops stationed in India, opposition leader Churchill questioned whether the consent of the Commonwealth nations had been sought in advance for this policy decision, or whether they were being asked to approve it after it had become a *fait accompli*. Attlee replied that consent had been obtained in advance. But this was not actually the case. Canada protested first, saying that consent had not been obtained in advance. Australia also complained, saying that at a time when the Commonwealth nations were discussing how to strengthen their participation in imperial decision-making, the government had made this important decision without first obtaining the consent of the Commonwealth nations. Thus, there was another verbal storm in the House of Commons, which was resolved only after much explanation. At the same time, it seems that the Commonwealth nations are exerting considerable indirect influence on the mother country's foreign policy. (Xueyan, dispatch from London, 30th)

Provisional University Students Want to Continue Their Education 108

Editor: Our school - the Shanghai Provisional University Preparatory Class Attached to the Special Shanghai Provisional University Preparatory Class of the Ministry of Education - completed its second semester exams on the 7th of this month. It can also be said that the Provisional University Preparatory Class will be eternally gone. Recalling the four months since the opening of the preparatory class, we have reviewed the entire middle school curriculum, and undergone two rigorous semester written exams. Although we students come from all directions, our goals are the same - hoping to be recommended to a national university. Now that the semester has ended, the Ministry of Education and the school authorities have not announced anything regarding the further education of our preparatory class students. Thinking of this, we envy the students who skipped grades during the puppet regime. Those who were in the same grade as us or lower in the past are now studying in their second or third year of university, and the Ministry of Education is very forgiving of these students, as evidenced by the screening measures. Now, the Shanghai Education Bureau has begun to conduct screening for graduates of secondary schools in the recovered areas, according to the order of the Ministry. We do not know if we will also have to undergo the same screening? We request that the Ministry of Education announce the two major issues of the recommendation of students from the Provisional University Preparatory Class Attached to the Shanghai Provisional University and the screening as soon as possible, so as to avoid students waiting too long and missing the date of the university entrance examination! (Wang Bomin, Cai Zhongzheng, Liu Dagui)

Hoping for Middle School Evening Classes 109

Editor: Universities such as Shanghai University and Soochow University have evening classes, purely for working youth, but they require a high school diploma. I am a primary school graduate, and I should go on to further education, but due to circumstances, I had to abandon my studies and go into business. But I still cannot forget my desire for education. Although I am supplementing my education in a tutoring night school, it is a school without a system. There must be many others with the same situation as me. Therefore, I hope that each university's evening classes will have a complete middle school evening class attached. Those who graduate from the middle school in the evening class can enter the university class, so that we, the general primary school graduates, can also study hard and obtain a bachelor's degree. I wonder if the school authorities can adopt this? (Luo Jiawei, Shanghai)

The Dispute Between Long-Term and Short-Term Workers 110

Mr. Editor:

We are laborers working at the Tongji Textile and Dyeing Factory at 20 Anda Road. For the past two months, we have consistently arrived early and left late, fulfilling our duties. Now, the factory has no shortage of goods, with vigorous imports and exports. However, on the morning of July 2nd at 9:00 AM, the factory suddenly dismissed over forty of us. At that time, we immediately appointed a representative to ask for the reason for the dismissal. They said that the factory has rules stipulating that workers who have been at the factory for three months are promoted to long-term workers. Since you have only been here for a little over two months, you are still considered temporary workers, and the factory can terminate your employment at any time.

However, according to the regulations of the Social Affairs Bureau, the compensation for temporary workers must exceed that of long-term workers by 35%. Yet, our compensation as temporary workers is only four-fifths of that of long-term workers. Furthermore, the factory is not lacking business. If it were lacking business and completely shut down, we would not make unreasonable demands, preferring to face unemployment.

At the time, we immediately requested the Third District Dyeing and Weaving Industry Labor Union to send representatives to demand reinstatement from the factory. The labor union sent members Xu Wenhua and Li Sixun to the factory to demand reinstatement again. The factory director, He Yutang, presented the following conditions to the labor union members: this group of workers, who entered the factory before June 30th, must have their past two months of work nullified, and they cannot continue from the later date to be promoted to long-term workers. Otherwise, they will definitely be dismissed.

We respectfully ask people from all walks of life for guidance. Is this reasoning correct? What will we do to survive after losing our jobs? (Tongji New Workers)

Unwilling to Be Ruled by the Reds 111

We are a group of refugees from Northern Jiangsu. Our hometowns have been occupied by the Communist army since the victory and are now called the "Liberated Areas." After experiencing the Communist army's policies of "three resources," "three equalizations," and "three clearances," tens of millions of our compatriots are in dire straits. We are unwilling to endure their oppression (which is fundamentally not allowed to exist) and have successively fled south, gathering in the Nanjing and Shanghai areas, numbering no less than three million people. The intermittent ceasefire negotiations, such as allowing the CCP to station two divisions in the Northern Jiangsu region, stationed in Huai'an and north of it, we firmly oppose. Because isn't this just like the era of the enemy puppets? Separating Huai'an into "Central China" and "North China" regions, to divide the whole and then return to the Communist Party's jurisdiction, we demand that the government preserve the unity of military and administrative orders in Jiangsu Province; not only Northern Jiangsu, but all parts of the country should also have the power to unify military and administrative orders. Although we refugees are currently receiving the government's attention and relief, as well as sympathy and donations from all sides, providing temporary comfort, it is not a long-term solution. We must eventually return home, and we ask the government and fair-minded people to assist us. (Refugees from Huai'an, Huaiyin, Lian'shui, Si'yang, Suqian, and Mudu Counties in Pudong, Zheng Qing, Shen Qicai, Xu Canwen, et al.)

The Voices of Public Toilet Management Workers 112

Recently, there have been reports that public toilets have increased the price of defecation three times in a row, increasing the burden on citizens. We, the workers managing public toilets, would like to offer an explanation and appeal to the authorities for assistance: (1) We workers purchase toilet paper for defecation from contractors, and after paying the contract price, what remains is barely enough to maintain our families. Outsiders are unaware of the truth and mistakenly believe that public toilets are absolutely free. This is a misunderstanding. (2) In the past few months, the cleaning department was responsible for assessing and paying sales fees, which were paid according to the actual situation. However, starting in June, the authorities changed their policy to focus on increasing revenue, contracting the public toilet department to merchants at a price about ten times higher. Merchants, whose purpose is to make a profit, pass on the contract price to the workers. Therefore, each public toilet pays tens of thousands of yuan, and it is difficult to bear this huge compensation without increasing the price of defecation. Therefore, we have made a slight increase. (3) From this day forward, all of us workers have been ordered by the Lei Bureau to reduce sales by 20 yuan each time. Not only can we not maintain our livelihoods with this, but we must also compensate with huge amounts of money. We are forced to appeal to the authorities and request: (1) Please adjust the selling price to 40 yuan. (2) Reduce the contract price by four-tenths. (3) Fix the long-term contract price and limit price changes within one year. In summary, we hope that the relevant authorities will adopt our requests. We are extremely grateful! (Public Toilet Paper Sales Management Workers of this city)

Social Services

Answers to Readers - Legal Advice 113

(1) Gao Junyong asks: My friend A lived with his adopted daughter-in-law B in the winter of 1927. Without marriage, they cohabited for five years and had a son. Later, in 1933, they became enemies because of economic pressure, causing B to abandon her husband and son and leave home without a trace. Later, in 1939, she cohabited with a pseudo-squad leader C and has been living together for seven years, without having any children. My friend A is very honest, but although he knows about this, he is afraid of C's power, so he has not dared to sue in court until now. Now, B is homesick (the son is already seventeen years old), has repented of the past, and is willing to reconcile. However, C is obstructing her from the middle, threatening her verbally, causing A great mental pain. Therefore, I am asking the following questions on his behalf, hoping that you can answer them in your column. I would be very grateful! 1. Although A and B were not formally married and there is no evidence (such as betrothal cards), they cohabited for five years and had a son. Can they be considered husband and wife in law? 2. A and B have not gone through the procedures for ending cohabitation and have been separated for fourteen years. Can the name of husband and wife still be established? 3. Is C guilty of occupying another man's wife? What kind of crime is it? However, they have been cohabiting for seven years. Can it be said that A has tacitly approved and obtained legal cohabitation? 4. Can A formally sue C for hindering the family?

[Lawyer Duanmu answers] 1. They cannot be considered husband and wife. 2. There is no name of husband and wife. 3. B is not a married woman. 4. A cannot sue C for hindering the family. 5. B cannot be charged with bigamy or adultery.

(2) Huang Yao asks: Zhang Jun's family has lived in a traditional single-story house (a total of three rooms) at No. X Changping Road for generations. From April 1940, he rented it to Jiang Jun for a term of four years (without a lease agreement). He had collected rent monthly for four years. In April 1944, Zhang Jun's children increased in number, and his own residence was not enough. He asked Jiang Jun to move out and take it back for his own use, not collecting rent until now for two years. However, Jiang Jun still makes excuses and refuses to move out, and repeated reminders have been ineffective. He had no choice but to apply to the Shanghai Municipal Housing Lease Management Committee for mediation, which was also unsuccessful. Now there are several questions: 1. Which articles of law has Jiang Jun violated in this case? Is there any conflict between Zhang Jun's facts and the law? 2. What evidence should Zhang Jun present to the court when he sues to take it back for his own use? 3. How should we deal with Jiang Jun's lies? 4. Is it possible for the court to rule that "the defendant continues to live there"? What is the reason? I have asked for your advice and would be grateful if you could provide a public reply.

[Lawyer Duanmu Kai answers] 1. Jiang Jun violated Article 450, Paragraph 1 of the Civil Code. 2, 4. Taking back for personal use requires proof from the police, self-governing organization, or housing lease management committee. 3. If Jiang Jun is lying, you must present evidence.

(3) Zhang Lide asks: A owns a large foreign-style house. During the enemy-puppet period, it was sold to a Japanese company. Because foreigners cannot obtain ownership of real estate in China, a Chinese B was used as the nominal buyer. The sales contract was kept by the company. After the victory, before the Japanese residents were sent to the concentration camp, A repurchased the house and sales contract from B at the original price and gave B a considerable reward, stipulating that if a problem occurred, B would claim to be the actual buyer. Now A has sold the house to a certain organization. (1) Is this property enemy property? (2) What is B's legal responsibility? (3) Is the sales contract between A and the organization valid? (4) Is the price obtained by A unjustly enriched? If it is unjustly enriched, who should it be returned to? (5) If A cannot hand over the price, what should be done?

[Lawyer Duanmu Kai answers] (1) Since it was purchased with funds from an enemy Japanese company, it is enemy property. (2) B has no right to dispose of the property. (3) The sales contract between A and the organization is not legally valid. (4) The price received by A from the organization should be returned to the original owner. If it cannot be returned, there is no choice but to seek a court decision.

Street Education 117

During the War of Resistance, "Military Affairs First"; during the period of national reconstruction, "Education First." Many educators have issued urgent appeals, calling for speeding up the restoration of the education sector, demanding that the authorities allocate more education funds, and people across the country have united to make efforts to relieve out-of-school children.

Indeed, how much work have the children done?

Tuition fees are so expensive that the majority of parents with meager incomes feel overwhelmed, and how many school authorities are truly teaching children well? Teachers' lives are difficult, and they have no choice but to exert their best efforts to teach part-time everywhere, so they are mentally exhausted during class, and revising homework is even more exhausting.

We sympathize with the teachers. We forgive their difficulties. But we also cannot deny a fact, which is that, under the current circumstances, children can really learn very little in school. We do not approve of turning innocent and lively children into hunchbacked and nearsighted little scholars. All we ask is that the school give them a healthy life, a pure atmosphere. The purpose of publishing these photos here is to draw everyone's attention - please take a look, is this kind of life healthy? Is it pure?

These are all innocent children! But on the streets, they learn to play cards and fight crickets. They don't have books that suit their tastes, so they sit quietly in front of small bookstores, calmly accepting the toxins of gods, monsters, superstitions, and pornography in those small books. They don't have appropriate places to exercise, so they kick soccer balls and play games on the crowded and messy street corners, and how many speeding cars in Shanghai threaten these small, lovely lives every day!

We are not qualified to condemn the children, they are innocent. We only hope that the millions of citizens of Shanghai will calmly think: have we fulfilled our responsibilities as parents? (Pingzhai)

Spring and Autumn

Literary Sensitivity 122

— Kai Yin

Literary workers are always at the forefront of the times, and the creation is a soul adventure. We say that literary workers must have a sensitivity different from ordinary people, and its significance lies in the fact that sensitivity is a sign of prescience. Without sensitivity, a writer cannot grasp the most tempting things in the vast life and express the most important things. Sensitivity is the intellectual antenna of literary workers.

Sensitivity and so-called "nervousness" are absolutely different. The former is a premonition of undiscovered things based on the correct position, while the latter is a kind of self-consciousness, a kind of morbid illusion. Usually, when self-consciousness develops too abnormally, it forms signs of nervousness. The literary sensitivity we are talking about should be the recognition of objective necessity through subjective and calm observation. Because of sensitivity, the writer's subject matter will never be exhausted. He will never live in the crowd in a muddled way, but will always retain a deep concern. If the literary worker himself is numb and indifferent to things, then his sensitivity is definitely not healthy.

Secondly, some people confuse the meaning of sensitivity with inspiration, which is wrong. Inspiration is extremely abstract. It is only the harmony of emotional development with the desire to write. Its main significance lies in the success of a creation because of the burning of the desire to write. But sensitivity is different. It is the pursuit of concrete things between the present and the future. It is in the observation of life, not in the practice of writing. Those who emphasize inspiration are mostly romantic writers. They think that when inspiration comes, ideas will flow like a spring, and then a great work is produced; but sensitivity is not like this. It is like a news reporter's nose. It can also predict the possible development of things that are still brewing, or it can obtain a line for interviewing news. Sensitivity works at any time in daily life. It requires profound observation, and without the guidance of sensitivity, failure is inevitable.

For example, Newton, because he saw an apple falling from a tree, most people would not pay attention to it, but he was surprised and researched the reason. This can be said to be a kind of sensitivity to natural phenomena, which is precious.

Writers, like social natural scientists, need a calm mind to observe things, analyze phenomena, and need a cautious and careful research attitude. Sensitivity is just one of the conditions.

Silhouette (Novel) (Part 2) 123

— Zhong Yi

Ru Ji exhaled a large mouthful of thick smoke, peering at Xiao Shi from within the smoke, remaining silent. Then, after taking four or five more puffs, he said weakly,

"I know, I know I shouldn't do this, but the environment doesn't allow me not to! I feel a strong force driving me; I desperately need that silhouette!" As he spoke, he nodded resolutely.

"..." Xiao Shi now began to feel that it was useless to try and dissuade him; because he had already stated that he "needed" that silhouette! He needed to eat; could you persuade him not to? More persuasion would not only fail to change his mind but might even strengthen his conviction, making it even more unshakable! So, he closed his eyes and pondered quietly, his forehead crisscrossed with wrinkles. For the moment, he seemed to have forgotten that a friend was sitting in the room, he was only concerned with engaging his own mind.

Ru Ji looked at his watch again, lazily picked up his hat, and seemed about to leave. He stuck the remaining short cigarette in his mouth, puffing it diligently, and said softly, "I'm sorry to have made you waste so much time for nothing, Xiao Shi. I feel quite relieved now, because the frustrations accumulated in my heart have been poured out and vented! Alas, but who knows what the future holds? If you don't mind the trouble, I think—I still want to borrow your ears as a tool to wash away my troubles! At this moment, I want to—"

Xiao Shi, in his state of contemplation, hadn't heard a word of Ru Ji's until Ru Ji uttered the words "I want," and then he awoke as if from a dream, quickly walking to Ru Ji's side, placing his hand on his shoulder, and said cheerfully,

"Hey, Ru Ji, I've found a solution! I can save you! I can make you happy!"

Ru Ji held his head high, playing with the smoke as usual, waiting a while before asking indifferently,

"Really?"

"Oh, would I lie to you?"

"Then please, what's your solution? Tell me."

Xiao Shi twitched his nose, holding Ru Ji's hand and saying,

"This... it's not convenient to reveal just yet, because you're too stubborn. If I told you, you might disagree, or be unwilling, and all that, so I think it's safer not to announce it! In short, Ru Ji, I vow to do my best to help you solve this problem! As for what steps to take, you don't need to worry about that!"

"No, please tell me!"

"No, I can't tell you! You lack patience! It's really late now, you should go home. I'll call you in a couple of days to discuss things!"

Xiao Shi's so-called "solution" was not really a clever plan. He was simply planning to shift Ru Ji's thoughts from Min Yu and the silhouette to somewhere else, to make him forget the silhouette and seek happiness and interest in other things! If such a solution could be realized, it would of course be extremely satisfactory; in fact, there was no other way to alleviate Ru Ji's pain! However, Ru Ji himself seemed to have tried this method before, and the result was failure. For example, he let work and reading occupy his time, he went to Wuxi, and so on, but the result was always an inability to break free, always unable to jump out of the walls built by painful memories!

Then, looking at it this way, this method has no effect, so how can Xiao Shi be so confident in telling him that he has a solution to save him? It turns out that Xiao Shi, while contemplating, carefully analyzed the matter and discovered the crux of Ru Ji's failure! He believed that Ru Ji's method—which was actually his own method—was absolutely flawless in principle. The reason for his failure was entirely due to the inappropriate choice of goals for shifting his thoughts, thinking that books, work, new environments, and so on, were lifeless things. Things without life, their ability to attract attention, was of course inevitably weaker than things with life and vitality! So, Xiao Shi was prepared to guide Ru Ji's thoughts towards a goal with life and vitality!

He remembered that on the day of his engagement, there was a young and beautiful Miss Sun Yun among the guests, who attracted the attention of all the guests present! This Miss Sun was a very close classmate of his fiancée. As for her appearance and figure, she was indeed worthy of the word "beautiful"! Miss Shi—his fiancée—was also beautiful, but Miss Shi's beauty was quiet, gentle, and virtuous, while Miss Sun's beauty was lively and light! Such a lively, intelligent, and beautiful Miss, no matter who saw her, could not help but envy her! So, Xiao Shi believed that if he introduced her to Ru Ji, Ru Ji would definitely not be able to resist her allure! At the same time, Ru Ji himself was also a fairly handsome young man; Miss Sun's beauty, paired with Ru Ji's handsomeness, seemed to be a perfect match!

However, before Ru Ji had seen her, before he had forgotten Min Yu, he was probably not going to agree to this proposal, because he was very stubborn. So, the only way was not to let him know in advance, and to see how he reacted after a sudden introduction? Was Min Yu's magic stronger, or was Miss Sun's temptation stronger? If it was the former, then of course he would continue to miss his lost Min Yu, if it was the latter, then he could turn back to the shore and approach Miss Sun! According to Xiao Shi's estimation, although Ru Ji was fond of Min Yu, she ultimately had no feelings for him, so his plan would definitely be victorious!

Miss Shi lived in a school dormitory, and only stayed at home two days a week. Originally, she was prepared not to live in the dormitory after she got engaged, but she thought that the home environment was too noisy and not suitable for studying, so she still decided to stay at school. Whenever she returned home on Saturday, Xiao Shi would go to the Shi's house to chat with her, and on Sunday, Miss Shi would come to Xiao Shi's house, or go out to play.

This Sunday, Xiao Shi agreed with Miss Shi to invite Miss Sun and Ru Ji to go to the movies together. Miss Shi naturally expressed her support for Xiao Shi's plan. They expected that in the cinema, going in would be two couples and two singles, but coming out would be two couples!

When Ru Ji arrived at the cinema, the other three had been waiting for a long time. Miss Shi and Miss Sun were waiting by the escalator inside because they disliked the dust at the entrance of the cinema, but Xiao Shi was afraid that Ru Ji would not be able to find them when he arrived, so he stood alone at the entrance waiting.

"Sorry, sorry, I'm late!" Ru Ji panted.

"It doesn't matter," Xiao Shi replied with a smile. "You don't need to apologize to me. It's true that you should apologize to them later!"

"Them? Who?" Ru Ji said with a smile, "Oh, I see, Miss Shi is here too, isn't she?"

"Yes... you'll understand in a moment, let's go in!"

Pushing open the glass door, Ru Ji's eyes scanned around, and suddenly he shouted softly,

"Silhouette! Silhouette!"

Xiao Shi was taken aback at first, then looked at Ru Ji's face and suddenly said,

"You remembered that silhouette again?"

"No, Xiao Shi, it's here! The silhouette is here, I've reunited with her!"

"Where? Where?" Xiao Shi asked anxiously.

"Standing by the escalator, wearing a pink short coat!... Alas, I want to go up! I want to..."

Xiao Shi was stunned listening to his words! He grabbed Ru Ji's sleeve, his lips trembling, unable to speak! After half a moment, he managed to squeeze out a sentence with great effort:

"That, that's my fiancée!" 3/5, 3/29. (The End)

Long Serial

Lovers Flying Together (90) 124

— Zhao Qingge

"Xiao Hua, let me introduce you to Mr. Dong Shaoling, the Chinese teacher at our school," Liu Ziyun said, pointing to the man. "His knowledge is very good, and you can learn a lot from him in the future. He is not only knowledgeable but also talented; he can play instruments, sing, and act! He goes to see your plays almost every day. He greatly admires your art."

Hearing this, Zhang Xuan widened his eyes, glared at Dong Shaoling, sneered, and said coldly,

"Mr. Dong is so knowledgeable and talented that our Xiao Hua is simply too good for him."

"Master!" Li Hua walked towards Zhang Xuan with a stern face. "It's getting late, you can go back." Saying this, she gestured for him to leave.

"What?" Zhang Xuan looked very resentful, and said with a sneer! "It's getting late, but the guest hasn't left yet, has he?"

Li Hua was simply furious and shouted sternly,

"Master!"

"Okay, my Ink Boss! Don't worry, I'm leaving now. Since you hate me, I'll go sit in the outer room, come on, let's warm up the voice for Little..." Saying this, Zhang Xuan picked up his Erhu and glared at Dong Shaoling again, then stumbled out.

"Mom, my master is so rude, I can't let him come to our house again!" Li Hua said angrily to Mrs. Mo.

"Tsk, tsk, tsk, that's just him, don't pay attention to him." Mrs. Mo comforted Li Hua, and then went out as well.

At this time, the Erhu sounded outside, and Li Yun sang: "Selling the Horse". Liu Ziyun and Dong Shaoling looked at each other silently. Dong Shaoling looked a little uncertain and kept gesturing for Liu Ziyun to leave, but Liu Ziyun refused to move, and gestured to stop Dong Shaoling.

"Mr. Liu! This, this is why I didn't want to tell... my identity," Li Hua said sadly after a moment of silence.

"Xiao Hua, I expected that you must have many difficulties in your heart. Come to school tomorrow and talk to me. Don't be so depressed, be careful you'll ruin your health." Liu Ziyun went over sympathetically, stroked Li Hua, and said comfortingly.

"Sigh!" Dong Shaoling sighed deeply, said nothing, put on his hat, and prepared to leave.

"Mr. Dong!" Li Hua looked up, with tears in her eyes, and said to him: "I'm really sorry!"

"It's nothing!" Dong Shaoling was also a little embarrassed. He urged Liu Ziyun again. "Let's go!"

Liu Ziyun then nodded, picked up his raincoat, and patted Li Hua.

"Don't be sad, come to school to play tomorrow!" After saying that, Liu Ziyun went out.

Free Talk

Hard Is the Road 127

— Shao Fu

The traffic situation in Shanghai, if it continues like this, will be a terrible future.

Taking the Route 1 trolleybus from the end of North Sichuan Road to Shanxi Road takes an average of 50 minutes, and the waiting time, from 10 minutes to half an hour, depends on your luck.

The chaotic, disorderly state of the roads is fully demonstrated on Nanjing Road and Beijing Road, making one suspect that they are fleeing or that enemy planes are attacking, otherwise how could there be such a hurried look.

Military trucks and jeeps crash around; three-wheeled vehicles and rickshaws weave around in the gaps;… we can't help but admire the bravery of these drivers, and even more admire their skills.

Many drivers are very proud, they don't take traffic violations seriously, they say, even if you drive a car without a license now, it's no big deal to be fined 1,000 yuan? Yes, compared to the old days when the concession would arrest you and put you in the Western prison for two days, it's really no big deal. Just two hours before I wrote this article, the rickshaw I was in crossed the Nanjing Road and Chengdu Road intersection under a red light, passing through two policemen without any trouble.

Shanghai makes newcomers dizzy, and traffic chaos is a major reason. It would be shameless of us to say that this is the face of urban prosperity!

Some people suggest banning three-wheeled vehicles and rickshaws, and we absolutely agree, but we hope that before the ban, transportation tools for millions of citizens to travel must be arranged first: and before this step, traffic management must be strict and thorough, don't just hold a few meetings, issue a declaration, post a few slogans, and have a few conductors decorating the intersections during the "movement" days, and then everything is back to normal.

We citizens silently pray that the municipal authorities will immediately take the most appropriate measures!

Resurrection 128

— Dongfang Jing

"Soviet scientists have found that 51 civilians who died have come back to life as a result of experiments."

In the past, people were divided into two major categories: living and dead. Between life and death, there is a clear boundary. Once you enter the "other world," you can never return to the human world—unless an incredible miracle occurs.

For most of them, the period of revival was very short, only a few hours or days. They eat, drink, talk, and even write letters, but the damage to vital organs ultimately cannot be saved.

Of the 51 people, 12 are still alive, living normal lives.

The method used by these Soviet scientists is very simple: after death, rescue as quickly as possible, injecting warm blood, mixed with adrenal compounds and glucose, into the brachial artery—the shortcut to the heart. Under high pressure, this mixture can cause the heart to contract, causing blood to flow from the arteries into the veins.

At the same time, doctors use artificial respiration to restore the dead person's breathing, which often needs to be continued for a long time, perhaps up to an hour after life is restored, until the patient can breathe freely.

The results of Soviet medical experiments tell us that the weakest part of the human body is not the heart, but the nervous system. It is the first to die from long-term anemia.

Dr. Negovsky announced to the world: "We cannot give up our efforts because the patient's heart and breathing have stopped, we should continue to fight for the patient's life, especially those who die suddenly… Hearts that have stopped beating can sometimes beat again."

Now, science has a different explanation for life and death. There is no definite distance between life and death. Even if a person enters the realm of death, he still has a chance to return to the living world.

This means that after you die, you still have a chance to come back to life. This is not just a sensational theory, but 51 people have already been saved from death using this new method.

Currently, to save a dead person, the time of death cannot be too long, about five minutes or so. But, the important thing is that dead people can be saved. Those who die from fainting, excessive bleeding, or other curable diseases have gained new life.

This resurrection technique was researched by Dr. Negovsky of the Soviet Ministry of Health and his deputies. Initially, they used this technique to save fallen soldiers, and now it is used on civilians. They also provide all data and technology to doctors in the United States and other countries.

From Life to Death in Several Stages

The basis of Negovsky's resurrection technique is that the various parts of the human body do not die at the same time. He discovered: "Death is not the sudden cessation of life; from life to death, there are several transitional stages."

Therefore, although the heart stops, other parts of the body may still be alive. A doctor can declare this person dead, but it is not "biological death" (all parts of the human body are dead), and he often has a chance to be resurrected.

There was a private in the Red Army named Zhirimanov who was seriously injured in the hip and had completely lost consciousness when he was taken to the hospital. He was carried to the operating table, but the situation was getting worse and worse. Finally, the heart stopped, breathing stopped, and nerve reflexes disappeared.

The surgeon routinely reported: "Death due to syncope and excessive bleeding."

At this time, Dr. Negovsky walked in. Three minutes later, he started working. One minute later, he started working. One minute later, Zhirimanov's heart began to beat; three minutes later, he began to breathe; within an hour, he regained consciousness.

Soon after, he fell asleep. Called his name, he opened his eyes and answered questions. He wanted water to drink. His breathing was normal and even, and his pulse was normal.

Today, Zhirimanov is doing very well, and he simply cannot believe that he is a person who has died once.

What Is the Afterlife Like?

A reporter asked him if he had seen anything interesting in the other world. Scratching his head, he apologized and replied: "Actually, I didn't see anything. At the moment of death, I had already lost consciousness, and I didn't regain consciousness until after the surgery. It was like having been anesthetized."

Dr. Negovsky said that the first thing dead people lose is consciousness; and the last thing to recover after resurrection is consciousness. The patient does not know the beginning of death, so he knows nothing about everything after death.

Zhirimanov is one of the 51 dead people saved by Dr. Negovsky. So these people all died because their internal organs or limbs were seriously injured, and ordinary rescue methods were ineffective.

Where Have the Fake Self-Defense Corps Helmets Gone? 129

— Cai Lin

During the period of occupation in this city, all the poor Shanghai citizens, in addition to bearing all kinds of exorbitant taxes, had to pay a "Baojia donation," and within the Baojia column, there were countless inexplicable donations. In short, nothing was spared, and everything from air defense and fire fighting to the tools used for mines, self-defense kiosks, and corps uniforms, all this was scraped from the people's heads, causing the people to be bruised and bleeding, and complaints were endless.

Many of the receivers after the victory seemed to focus on the big picture, thus ignoring the small things, just like the large number of self-defense corps helmets in the city mentioned in this article, which the public has completely forgotten, is this not sad?

Moreover, these helmets are now becoming waste, so why not use them? Besides, everything belonging to the public, whether it's a blade of grass or a tree, should be returned to the public without exception. What I mean is that this large number of helmets should be investigated by the military organs of this city, tasking the Baojia chiefs to pursue them, ordering those who hide them to hand them over, and those who have lost them must compensate according to the market price, because they are useless to the possessors, and many comrades in the army are still lacking helmets, so taking them back and returning them to the public is not troublesome, so why not do it?

A Few Words

The Sale of Jiang's Case Materials Is a Long Way Off 130

— Wuling Ren

The High Court recently pronounced judgments on many traitor cases, with many sentences ranging from two to three years, which may have made many people feel relieved, but it must also have made many people feel chilled.

Boy Scouts at the North Railway Station persuade travelers to get vaccinations, even begging, which shows the low level of knowledge of the general public. Some people are afraid of trouble and small pain, but they are not afraid of life-threatening dangers, and some people are probably even unaware of the meaning of vaccination, which is even more pitiful.

The previous few hurricanes in the Pacific were fortunately extinguished, allowing Shanghai to avoid being attacked, but as soon as one wind disappears, another wind rises. Whether Shanghai can always be safe is still unknown. The news of hurricanes existing for one more day means that the people of Shanghai will have one more day of worry.

Regarding the materials involved in Jiang Gongmei's case, many of them have already rotted. According to reports, the authorities concerned "will draw up detailed methods in the coming days and present them to the commander for approval before unsealing and selling them." The news of the rot of Jiang's case materials seems to have been seen as early as two months ago, and now we are only hearing about the submission of the application for unsealing and sale, but "in the coming days," "will," "draw up," "present for approval"... it seems that it will have to go through several stages, and even if "approval is granted for sale," I am afraid that this batch of materials will have reached the stage of "waste utilization."

The wife of Wu Shibao, the demon of "No. 76," defended her deceased husband in court, saying that Wu had never fired a gun or killed anyone. Indeed, I also believe that Wu Shibao would not go to the execution ground to personally shoot "criminals."

Serialized

Dedicated to My Deceased Wife, Feng Jun (13) 131

— Zhou Shoujuan

Your spirit of urging me to work hard and showing consideration for the servants was something no ordinary housewife possessed. Every day you would rise before dawn, often ahead of Auntie Ye, first sweeping the bedroom. Then you would go downstairs to the kitchen, light the briquette stove, and then boil water to cook porridge, so that the children could get up, wash, and have breakfast without being late for teaching, studying, or work. When Auntie Ye went to the market for groceries, you would busy yourself selecting and washing rice, preparing everything in advance, and then have your own breakfast, sometimes even forgetting it and skipping a meal. Seeing that you ate little and had so much to do, and that you were working so hard, I always advised you to rest more. You would reply, "Auntie Ye can't manage everything alone. The children will be back for lunch, so I want to prepare everything early, so I can feel at ease." I couldn't convince you otherwise, so I had to let you be. After a short rest in the afternoon, you would busy yourself with needlework, putting on your glasses and working tirelessly, even mending our torn clothes and unraveling shoes and socks. Although the children had all grown up and wore leather shoes outside, the cloth-soled shoes they wore at home were all made by you. Over the past twenty-nine years, including those for my mother, you must have made thousands of pairs. Making the uppers was not considered difficult, but the fine, dense stitching of the soles was both laborious and time-consuming, even causing calluses to form between the two fingers that held the needle. In short, you were always trying to save me money and plan for me, day in and day out for twenty-nine years. As for entertainment, during these nine years of national crisis, it was practically nonexistent. Sometimes, because my mother, your mother, and your aunt all loved to play mahjong, you would reluctantly join in, which for you was simply an obligation and not entertainment.

Last winter, our family had already decided to move back to our old home in Suzhou. I repeatedly invited you to go out and see a technicolor movie and have a Western meal that you loved, but you declined time and again, saying, "Dear, save your money. Let me rest at home; you go by yourself." When you did go out, the farthest you would go was to your mother's house on Dihua Road. You wouldn't even venture into the Jing'an Temple area, saying, "Once I go there and see the dazzling shop windows, I can't help but spend your money." Once, the newspaper office sent over several thousand dollars in manuscript fees. I casually handed them to you, and you took them in your hands, and tears welled up in your eyes. You sobbed, "Dear, this is what you earned with your heart's blood over the past month. How can I bear to spend it?" I quickly said, "Writing this kind of article is easy, it doesn't take much effort. Besides, since you are so considerate of me, I would be willing to pour out my heart's blood!" After much persuasion, you finally accepted.
